Chief Yamarz

**Chief Yamarz** is an [Orc](/wiki/Skyrim:Orc "Skyrim:Orc") [warrior](/wiki/Skyrim:GuardOrc1H "Skyrim:GuardOrc1H") and the chief of the accursed [Orc stronghold](/wiki/Skyrim:Orc_Strongholds "Skyrim:Orc Strongholds") of [Largashbur](/wiki/Skyrim:Largashbur "Skyrim:Largashbur"), located in [the Rift](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Rift "Skyrim:The Rift"), east of [Avanchnzel](/wiki/Skyrim:Avanchnzel "Skyrim:Avanchnzel"). He is generally unpleasant and displays many traits not normally associated with Orcs such as a conniving nature and an aversion to battle. It is never fully explained why [Malacath](/wiki/Lore:Malacath "Lore:Malacath") cursed his tribe, but it's implied that Yamarz's weaknesses as leader are a reflection of the curse itself. This would help explain why Malacath charges Yamarz alone with the task of slaying the leader of the [giant](/wiki/Skyrim:Giant "Skyrim:Giant") tribe that has defiled his shrine.

Yamarz is clad in a complete set of Orcish equipment. This includes the [cuirass](/wiki/Skyrim:Orcish_Armor "Skyrim:Orcish Armor"), a pair of [gauntlets](/wiki/Skyrim:Orcish_Gauntlets "Skyrim:Orcish Gauntlets"), a pair of [boots](/wiki/Skyrim:Orcish_Boots "Skyrim:Orcish Boots"), and a [helmet](/wiki/Skyrim:Orcish_Helmet "Skyrim:Orcish Helmet"). He is equipped with a leveled [war axe](/wiki/Skyrim:War_Axe "Skyrim:War Axe") and a leveled [shield](/wiki/Skyrim:Shield "Skyrim:Shield"), both of which can be up to Orcish quality.

## Related Quests

- **[The Cursed Tribe](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Cursed_Tribe "Skyrim:The Cursed Tribe")**: Help lift the curse placed on the [Orcs](/wiki/Skyrim:Orc "Skyrim:Orc") of [Largashbur](/wiki/Skyrim:Largashbur "Skyrim:Largashbur") by [Malacath](/wiki/Lore:Malacath "Lore:Malacath").

### The Cursed Tribe

When first spoken to:

:   *"Curses aren't enough, now I must suffer you too? What is it?"*
:   *"Why are you here, outsider?"*

:   :   **I'm just here to help.**
    :   *"Oh, of course! Because Malacath would take pity on us if only a useless outsider would lend a hand."*
    :   *"Yes, because a worthless City Orc is just what we've been waiting for. Finally, we're saved!"*

:   :   **How long has this been going on?**
    :   *"Weeks? Longer? It feels like an age has gone by. I haven't slept in so long."*

As you enter the [Largashbur Longhouse](/wiki/Skyrim:Largashbur_Longhouse "Skyrim:Largashbur Longhouse") with Atub:

:   **Atub:** *"It is time, Yamarz."*
:   **Yamarz:** *"You bring an outsider here, and now insist I call on Malacath for help, when he has clearly forsaken me? You try my patience, Atub."*
:   **Atub:** *"Doing nothing will not grant our tribe relief from this curse. We must try."*
:   **Yamarz:** *"Grrr. Fine, let's get this over with."*

Atub and Yamarz will then leave the longhouse and begin the ritual to speak to Malacath:

:   **Atub**: *"Now, we begin the ritual... Great Malacath, we beseech you, aid us in our time of need..."*
:   **Yamarz**: *"Why are we bothering with this?"*
:   **Malacath**: *"You pathetic weakling!"*
:   **Yamarz**: *"What's that?"*
:   **Atub**: *"Malacath has heard my pleas! He speaks to us!"*
:   **Malacath**: *"You dare summon me, Yamarz?"*
:   **Yamarz**: *"What? What is this?"*
:   **Malacath**: *"You don't deserve to call yourself an Orc! You're weak, you're small, and you're an embarrassment! You let giants... Giants!... overrun my shrine. Bring me their leader's club as an offering, and I might release you from this curse!"*
:   **Atub**: *"So it will be. Malacath has spoken, Yamarz. Your path is clear."*
:   **Yamarz**: *"Very well. You, outsider, come here! I want a word."*

When spoken to:

:   *"This is all your fault, you know. I'm stuck fighting a giant now, thanks to you. So you're going to help me. You're going with me, and you're going to make sure I don't have any trouble reaching that giant. Don't worry, I'll make it worth your while."*

:   :   **Fighting the giant isn't my job.**
    :   *"Thanks to you, I've just been issued a challenge in front of my whole tribe, by a Daedric Prince, no less. I can't ignore that. I didn't say I wouldn't fight the giant. I just said you're going to help me get to it. Meet me outside Fallowstone Cave. You clear the way to the giant for me, and I'll make sure you get paid for it."*

:   :   **What do you want me to do?**
    :   *"This giant... It's not the only thing in Fallowstone Cave. Getting to it isn't going to be easy. You're going to clear a path to the giant, so I can conserve my strength. I'll make sure you're paid for it. So you meet me at Fallowstone Cave, and we'll get this over with. I can have my tribe back, and you can... You can leave us alone."*

At Fallowstone Cave:

:   *"Let's just get this over with."*
:   *"If there's a chance this will save me, then I'm taking it."*
:   *"I'll lead the way, but you'd better back me up."*

In the Giant's Grove:

:   *"All right, I'll go kill this giant. Unless, of course, you'd like to make some extra gold."*

:   :   **What do you mean?**
    :   *"I'm tired, I haven't slept well in weeks. You kill the giant, bring me the hammer. We go back to Largashbur, I tell everyone I did it. You keep your mouth shut, and I pay you. Handsomely."*

        :   **Okay, I'll do it.**
        :   *"Good. I'll be waiting right here."*

:   :   **No, you're supposed to do it.**
    :   *"Fine, then wait here. This should only take a second."*

Returning to him with the hammer:

:   *"Excellent work. You have a true fighting spirit. Did that better than I could have. Of course, I can't let you leave here alive. Wouldn't want anyone finding out."*

He will then turn hostile and must be killed.

### Unused

Chief Yamarz has quite a bit of unused dialogue related to (what appears to be) a different start for the quest The Cursed Tribe.

:   **I understand you need help.**
:   *"Atub! Meddlesome woman... You would help us? Help me? Tell me, outsider. Can you banish spirits? For that is what I need."*

:   :   **I'm sorry, what?**
    :   *"Spirits! Ghosts! I am cursed, haunted, and I can do nothing. Can you fix that? Of course you cannot. No one can. It is my lot as Chief of this tribe, and so I suffer quietly."*

:   :   **What kind of spirits?**
    :   *"The kind that curse you, haunt you in the dead of night. There is nothing you can do, nothing anyone can do. Shagrol, once the leader of this tribe, unhappy with his demise, has dealt with Malacath himself to curse me, curse us all."*

Regardless of which option you chose, you would then follow up with:

:   **There must be something I can do.**
:   *"You? An outsider? I'd sooner slit my own throat than accept help from you. To even consider it would be such a sign of weakness that I might as well abandon my tribe now."*

:   :   **You have to do this yourself?**
    :   *"I am the one cursed by Malacath. It is my burden. I bear it, and continue to lead, and the others see how strong I am. That is how I rule."*

:   :   :   **A truly strong chief would break the curse, not suffer from it.**
        :   *"Hrmph. Breaking a curse is not a simple thing. It is dangerous. But... To have won against Malacath himself... That would be seen as real power."*

:   :   :   :   **So use me to help you break this curse.**
            :   *"You persist? Fine. You go tell Malacath to lift this curse from me. See how well he listens to you. Offer yourself up as a sacrifice while you're there."*

:   :   **I could help you in secret.**
    :   *"Are you blind, or just stupid? You think the tribe has not seen you talking to me? You think they would not know? Do not mistake our life for one of stupidity. It would be the last mistake you make."*

:   :   :   **Having an outsider do your bidding might seem powerful...**
        :   *"Perhaps... Perhaps it might. If nothing else, you could be an excellent sacrifice to Malacath. You really want to help? You go offer yourself at Malacath's Shrine. Petition him for help. He might not devour you whole."*

You would then be sent to Atub in order to further the quest. Yamarz has no further unused upon your return, however. Notably, this unused dialogue adresses Yamarz's curse and where it came from, while this is never elaborated upon in the final game.

## Bugs

- If Yamarz is kept pacified, The Cursed Tribe will still complete but won't acknowledge he is still alive.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 1.2.7, addresses this issue. Magic effect `InfluenceAggDownFFAimedArea` has been modified to make Yamarz immune to Pacify and other spells which use this effect.
- Yamarz's sleep package can't activate due to it being blocked by his general sandbox package.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 2.0.4, fixes this bug.
- When Yamarz says "It's not the only thing in Fallowstone Cave", the actual audio instead states "It's not the only thing in **the** Fallowstone Cave".
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 2.0.4, fixes this bug.

# Skyrim:Child

## Overview

Lars Battle-Born, a typical child

**Children** are young inhabitants of Skyrim that can be found in various places throughout the game world, most commonly in major cities and towns. They are not playable, and they cannot be killed. Only human [races](/wiki/Skyrim:Races "Skyrim:Races") ([Breton](/wiki/Skyrim:Breton "Skyrim:Breton"), [Nord](/wiki/Skyrim:Nord "Skyrim:Nord"), [Imperial](/wiki/Skyrim:Imperial "Skyrim:Imperial"), and [Redguard](/wiki/Skyrim:Redguard "Skyrim:Redguard")) have children present in the game; no elven or beast races offspring are encountered.

## Traits

- Height: 0.8000
- Weight: 1.0000
- No added spells or other abilities
- Cannot be harmed; attacks only cause visual injuries and can make a child flee and also count as an [assault](/wiki/Skyrim:Crime "Skyrim:Crime")
- Share the same starting [skills](/wiki/Skyrim:Skills "Skyrim:Skills") as their parents

## Gameplay

Although children can be interacted with via quests, dialogue, and various games ([tag](/wiki/Skyrim:Tag,_you%27re_it! "Skyrim:Tag, you're it!"), [hide and seek](/wiki/Skyrim:Hide_and_Seek_(game) "Skyrim:Hide and Seek (game)")), their most striking feature is that they cannot be harmed or killed. They also cannot be targeted for most other actions, including [pickpocketing](/wiki/Skyrim:Pickpocket "Skyrim:Pickpocket") and [feeding](/wiki/Skyrim:Vampirism#feeding "Skyrim:Vampirism"). Also, you cannot increase combat or destruction skills by using children as a target. Children will never engage in battle and will always flee at the first sign of a fight, however, if you use the [Rage](/wiki/Skyrim:Rage "Skyrim:Rage") [spell](/wiki/Skyrim:Spells "Skyrim:Spells") on a child they will engage in fighting. If children see you committing a [crime](/wiki/Skyrim:Crime "Skyrim:Crime"), they will report it to the nearest adult.

Children are present in the game world for increased realism and immersion but the game developers most likely opted for the "immortal" mechanic in order to avoid any "child-killing" controversy. For this reason, children were not included in either *[Morrowind](/wiki/Morrowind:Morrowind "Morrowind:Morrowind")* or *[Oblivion](/wiki/Oblivion:Oblivion "Oblivion:Oblivion")* (although the idea was brought up for the latter). They were finally featured in *Skyrim*; though, as stated, they are given special treatment.

## List of child NPCs and their locations

There are a total of 38 children in Skyrim (3 Bretons, 3 Imperials, 3 Redguards and 29 Nords). The *[Hearthfire](/wiki/Skyrim:Hearthfire "Skyrim:Hearthfire")* add-on adds a total of 4 more children (1 from each of the four mentioned races). The *[Dragonborn](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragonborn "Skyrim:Dragonborn")* add-on adds 1 more Nord child. [Creation Club](/wiki/Skyrim:Creation_Club "Skyrim:Creation Club") content adds 2 more Nord children.

| [Kayd](/wiki/Skyrim:Kayd "Skyrim:Kayd") | [Redguard](/wiki/Skyrim:Redguard "Skyrim:Redguard") | Male | [Beirand](/wiki/Skyrim:Beirand "Skyrim:Beirand") | [Sayma](/wiki/Skyrim:Sayma "Skyrim:Sayma") | [Bits and Pieces](/wiki/Skyrim:Bits_and_Pieces "Skyrim:Bits and Pieces") | [Solitude](/wiki/Skyrim:Solitude "Skyrim:Solitude") | No |  |
| Lavinia[†](#intnote_Dead) | unknown | Female | [Mathies](/wiki/Skyrim:Mathies "Skyrim:Mathies") | [Indara Caerellia](/wiki/Skyrim:Indara_Caerellia "Skyrim:Indara Caerellia") | None (buried in the Falkreath cemetery) | [Falkreath](/wiki/Skyrim:Falkreath "Skyrim:Falkreath") | No | See **[Ill Met By Moonlight](/wiki/Skyrim:Ill_Met_By_Moonlight "Skyrim:Ill Met By Moonlight")** |

[†](#note_Dead)Deceased (or undead), either initially or as a result of quest events.

[‡](#note_Adopt)"Yes" means they can be adopted immediately. "No" means they can never be adopted. "If orphan" means they can be adopted if their parent(s) are killed. (They will be moved to the Honorhall Orphanage in [Riften](/wiki/Skyrim:Riften "Skyrim:Riften") if this occurs.) Note that some parents may be essential and unkillable until after certain related quests have been completed.

## Adoption HF

See the [Adoption](/wiki/Skyrim:Adoption "Skyrim:Adoption") page.

## Notes

- In the [Creation Kit](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Creation_Kit "Skyrim Mod:Creation Kit") they are counted as a separate race, similar to how [Dremora](/wiki/Skyrim:Dremora "Skyrim:Dremora") and the [elders](/wiki/Skyrim:Elder "Skyrim:Elder") are treated.
- Despite being unkillable, children do have the "zombie grunt" and death sound files typical of humanoid reanimated targets, but you cannot hear them in normal gameplay.
- If you cast a spell near a child (including those you've adopted), he/she will respond by asking you to make them [invisible](/wiki/Skyrim:Invisibility_(effect) "Skyrim:Invisibility (effect)"). Unfortunately, you will not be able to do this (as there is no targeted invisibility spell in the game), so they will be disappointed when you refuse. Male children seem to ask about being made invisible far more than female children, however.
  - On the PC version, you can give yourself a spell *Fade Other* by using the console command: `player.addspell 28532`
  - You have the option to lie, and then pass a speech check (Lie). They will then begin acting like ghosts and start "finally having fun around here."
- There are some inconsistencies with the races of the children and their parents. [Fjotra](/wiki/Skyrim:Fjotra "Skyrim:Fjotra"), a [Nord](/wiki/Skyrim:Nord "Skyrim:Nord") child, has [Breton](/wiki/Skyrim:Breton "Skyrim:Breton") parents, [Enmon](/wiki/Skyrim:Enmon "Skyrim:Enmon") and [Mena](/wiki/Skyrim:Mena "Skyrim:Mena"). [Minette Vinius](/wiki/Skyrim:Minette_Vinius "Skyrim:Minette Vinius"), a Nord child, has an [Imperial](/wiki/Skyrim:Imperial "Skyrim:Imperial") father and an Imperial brother, [Corpulus Vinius](/wiki/Skyrim:Corpulus_Vinius "Skyrim:Corpulus Vinius") and [Sorex Vinius](/wiki/Skyrim:Sorex_Vinius "Skyrim:Sorex Vinius"), respectively. They might be results of an adoption.
- Adoption was originally developed as part of the [Game Jam](/wiki/Skyrim:Game_Jam "Skyrim:Game Jam").
- Children cannot be killed, not even by using the [console](/wiki/Skyrim:Console "Skyrim:Console"), though they can be [disabled](/wiki/Skyrim:Console#Targeted_Commands "Skyrim:Console").
- With the [Hearthfire](/wiki/Skyrim:Hearthfire "Skyrim:Hearthfire") [add-on](/wiki/Skyrim:Add-ons "Skyrim:Add-ons"), children's clothes can now be found and bought. They will appear in the "Miscellaneous" section of your inventory, though, not the "Apparel" section.
- The Redguard children appear very light skinned compared to other Redguards, this could be a mistake but is likely due to limitations on how children are implemented into the game.
- There are no [Beastfolk](/wiki/Lore:Beastfolk "Lore:Beastfolk") or [Elven](/wiki/Lore:Elves "Lore:Elves") children seen in the game.

## Bugs

Example of a child scaling to adult size

- All children in the game may appear in just their underwear, or may switch to underwear after being given new clothes as a gift.
- If you fast travel while playing a game of tag with children, it may cause the children to travel with you and wander off in random directions.
- Adopted children may disappear temporarily rather than showing up in their respective beds or just stand near their bed. **?**
- A dialogue line referring to the [Gildergreen](/wiki/Lore:Gildergreen "Lore:Gildergreen") in [Whiterun](/wiki/Skyrim:Whiterun "Skyrim:Whiterun") can be spoken by any child in any city due to a missing condition check.
  -  The [Unofficial Hearthfire Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Hearthfire_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Hearthfire Patch"), version 1.1.2, fixes this bug.
- The child beds in your [player-built house](/wiki/Skyrim:Construction "Skyrim:Construction") may not be marked as owned by the children, making it possible for the grown-ups to use them as well.
  -  The [Unofficial Hearthfire Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Hearthfire_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Hearthfire Patch"), version 2.0.2, fixes this bug.
- During the [Civil War](/wiki/Skyrim:Civil_War "Skyrim:Civil War") battles in Whiterun, Solitude, or Windhelm, it is possible for adopted children currently living in those cities to be transported back to their editor locations due to the AI package CWCitizensFleeSandboxEditorLocationLockDoors.
  -  The [Unofficial Hearthfire Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Hearthfire_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Hearthfire Patch"), version 2.0.3, addresses this issue. This package will now have a condition blocking it from taking effect on members of the BYOHRelationshipAdoptionFaction so the kids will instead flee to your house under the control of the proper quest for this purpose.
- [Hroki](/wiki/Skyrim:Hroki "Skyrim:Hroki") is the only adult in the game that is assigned the "child" class, though it is more of an oddity than anything else since it doesn't actually make her a child or invulnerable as they are.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 2.0.4, addresses this issue. Hroki is now part of the "citizen" class.
- If you [get married](/wiki/Skyrim:Marriage "Skyrim:Marriage"), your adopted children may attend the ceremony, but won't have any dialogue audio.
  -  The [Unofficial Hearthfire Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Hearthfire_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Hearthfire Patch"), version 2.1.3, addresses this issue. New dialogue lines for the children have been created.
- Helgi's voice lacks the ghost effect used by other spirits.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Legendary Edition Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Legendary_Edition_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Legendary Edition Patch"), version 3.0.1, fixes this bug.
- Several children either don't own the beds assigned to them or were assigned beds of the wrong size so they just sandbox near them all night.
  - The [Unofficial Skyrim Special Edition Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Special_Edition_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Special Edition Patch"), version 4.0.8, fixes this bug.
- Children who interact with certain in-game elements such as [forges](/wiki/Skyrim:Forge "Skyrim:Forge") can scale up to adult size, and then become stuck in this state permanently.

# Skyrim:Chillfurrow Farm

## Overview

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| |  |  | | --- | --- | | [SR-mapicon-Wheat Mill.png](/wiki/File:SR-mapicon-Wheat_Mill.png) | Wheat Mill: Chillfurrow Farm ([view on map](https://gamemap.uesp.net/sr/?world=Skyrim&centeron=Chillfurrow+Farm)) | | |

| Region | |
| [Whiterun Hold](/wiki/Skyrim:Whiterun_Hold "Skyrim:Whiterun Hold") | |

| East of [Whiterun](/wiki/Skyrim:Whiterun "Skyrim:Whiterun") | |

| # of [Cooking Pots/Spits](/wiki/Skyrim:Cooking "Skyrim:Cooking") | 1 |
| # of [Wood Chopping Blocks](/wiki/Skyrim:Chop_Wood "Skyrim:Chop Wood") | 1 |
| # of [Stone Quarries](/wiki/Skyrim:Quarried_Stone "Skyrim:Quarried Stone")[HF](/wiki/Skyrim:Hearthfire "Skyrim:Hearthfire") | 1 |

Chillfurrow Farm with Whiterun in the background

**Chillfurrow Farm** is a small farm just outside of [Whiterun](/wiki/Skyrim:Whiterun "Skyrim:Whiterun"), owned by [Nazeem](/wiki/Skyrim:Nazeem "Skyrim:Nazeem"). It is located south of [Battle-Born Farm](/wiki/Skyrim:Battle-Born_Farm "Skyrim:Battle-Born Farm").

Despite technically being Nazeem's property, he is always absent. The daily maintenance of the farm is in the hands of his employee, [Wilmuth](/wiki/Skyrim:Wilmuth "Skyrim:Wilmuth"), who also lives in the farmhouse. A [Whiterun Guard](/wiki/Skyrim:Whiterun_Guard "Skyrim:Whiterun Guard") will look after the farm around the clock, and another guard will cross the front yard several times a day. It consists of one zone, *[Chillfurrow Farm](#Chillfurrow_Farm)*.

## Residents

| Residents |
| --- |
| [Wilmuth](/wiki/Skyrim:Wilmuth "Skyrim:Wilmuth") |

### Exterior

| Crops | Plants | Animals | Other |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| 10 [Cabbage](/wiki/Skyrim:Cabbage "Skyrim:Cabbage")  7 [Wheat](/wiki/Skyrim:Wheat "Skyrim:Wheat") | 3 [Purple Mountain Flower](/wiki/Skyrim:Purple_Mountain_Flower "Skyrim:Purple Mountain Flower")  1 [Tundra Cotton](/wiki/Skyrim:Tundra_Cotton "Skyrim:Tundra Cotton") | 2 [Chicken](/wiki/Skyrim:Chicken "Skyrim:Chicken")  1 [Cow](/wiki/Skyrim:Cow "Skyrim:Cow") | 1 [Chickens' Nest](/wiki/Skyrim:Chicken%27s_Egg "Skyrim:Chicken's Egg") |

### Chillfurrow Farm

Inside Chillfurrow Farm

Farm owner [Nazeem](/wiki/Skyrim:Nazeem "Skyrim:Nazeem") is reputed to be an arrogant snob among the citizens of Whiterun, but has definitely provided his employee, [Wilmuth](/wiki/Skyrim:Wilmuth "Skyrim:Wilmuth"), with some luxurious surroundings. The front door opens to the sight of the traditional huge fireplace with two [cooking spits](/wiki/Skyrim:Cooking_Spit "Skyrim:Cooking Spit") and a small table with some common books. Above the fireplace hang three samples of [dried frost mirriam](/wiki/Skyrim:Dried_Frost_Mirriam "Skyrim:Dried Frost Mirriam"), three [garlic braids](/wiki/Skyrim:Garlic_Braid "Skyrim:Garlic Braid"), and two fresh [salmon](/wiki/Skyrim:Salmon_(dead) "Skyrim:Salmon (dead)"). In the southeastern corner is a small table with two bottles of [wine](/wiki/Skyrim:Wine "Skyrim:Wine") and a large dinner table with some food, including [grilled leeks](/wiki/Skyrim:Grilled_Leeks "Skyrim:Grilled Leeks"), a [salmon steak](/wiki/Skyrim:Salmon_Steak "Skyrim:Salmon Steak"), an [apple pie](/wiki/Skyrim:Apple_Pie "Skyrim:Apple Pie"), three [tomatoes](/wiki/Skyrim:Tomato "Skyrim:Tomato"), and another bottle of wine. The northeastern corner has a food sack and a food barrel, and on top of the latter, an [eidar cheese wheel](/wiki/Skyrim:Eidar_Cheese_Wheel "Skyrim:Eidar Cheese Wheel") and a [goat cheese wheel](/wiki/Skyrim:Goat_Cheese_Wheel "Skyrim:Goat Cheese Wheel"). While the nearby cupboard contains clutter, the shelves above have a head of [cabbage](/wiki/Skyrim:Cabbage "Skyrim:Cabbage"), a chunk of [venison](/wiki/Skyrim:Venison "Skyrim:Venison"), and some [horse meat](/wiki/Skyrim:Horse_Meat "Skyrim:Horse Meat") on display. A small working desk decorates the southwestern corner, with two [honey nut treats](/wiki/Skyrim:Honey_Nut_Treat "Skyrim:Honey Nut Treat") in a bowl and several books. Underneath the tabletop is an end table with clutter, on the floor, a pair of [boots](/wiki/Skyrim:Boots#000209a5 "Skyrim:Boots"). A food sack is leaning against a set of shelves along the western wall with even more books.

An entrance to a small storage unit can be found next to the fireplace and it contains six food sacks, a goat cheese wheel on top of a barrel, and a wardrobe with clothes. On top of the wardrobe sits a piece of [dog meat](/wiki/Skyrim:Dog_Meat "Skyrim:Dog Meat") and a [coin purse](/wiki/Skyrim:Coin_Purse "Skyrim:Coin Purse"). The bedroom contains Wilmuth's owned bed along with a handy keg and a [goblet](/wiki/Skyrim:Goblet "Skyrim:Goblet") next to his pillow. The end table underneath contains clutter, the sack underneath the bed contains food, and the [chest](/wiki/Skyrim:Chest "Skyrim:Chest") is non-respawning, unlocked, and contains leveled items. Adjacent to the bed, along the northern wall, is a dresser with clothes, with a bottle of [alto wine](/wiki/Skyrim:Alto_Wine "Skyrim:Alto Wine"), a coin purse, an [iron sword](/wiki/Skyrim:Iron_Sword "Skyrim:Iron Sword"), and a copy of the [One-handed](/wiki/Skyrim:One-handed "Skyrim:One-handed") skill book *[The Importance of Where](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Importance_of_Where "Skyrim:The Importance of Where")* on top.

## Notes

- All dressers, end tables, and cupboards in the location are [non-respawning](/wiki/Skyrim:Respawning "Skyrim:Respawning") and safe to store items in.
-  Version 2.1.1 of the [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch") marks the sacks, bucket, and pitchfork outside of the building as owned by the farm.

## Bugs

- The [grain mill](/wiki/Skyrim:Grain_Mill "Skyrim:Grain Mill") on the property was supposed to be able to produce [sacks of flour](/wiki/Skyrim:Sack_of_Flour "Skyrim:Sack of Flour") with [Hearthfire](/wiki/Skyrim:Hearthfire "Skyrim:Hearthfire") installed. However, the one at Chillfurrow Farm doesn't work.
- Nazeem was supposed to visit this farm every Loredas and Sundas at 12pm, but his patrol package is set to 'any' meaning it will always take precedence.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 1.2.2, fixes this bug.

# Skyrim:Chillwind Depths

## Overview

Chillwind Depths

**Chillwind Depths** is a small [cave](/wiki/Skyrim:Caves "Skyrim:Caves") south of [Dragon Bridge](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Bridge "Skyrim:Dragon Bridge") containing [Falmer](/wiki/Skyrim:Falmer "Skyrim:Falmer"), [chaurus](/wiki/Skyrim:Chaurus "Skyrim:Chaurus"), and [frostbite spiders](/wiki/Skyrim:Frostbite_Spider "Skyrim:Frostbite Spider"). It contains only one zone, *[Chillwind Depths](#Chillwind_Depths)*.

It is the largest single source of [bleeding crown](/wiki/Skyrim:Bleeding_Crown "Skyrim:Bleeding Crown"), [blisterwort](/wiki/Skyrim:Blisterwort "Skyrim:Blisterwort"), [imp stool](/wiki/Skyrim:Imp_Stool "Skyrim:Imp Stool"), [Namira's rot](/wiki/Skyrim:Namira%27s_Rot "Skyrim:Namira's Rot"), and [white cap](/wiki/Skyrim:White_Cap "Skyrim:White Cap").

### Exterior

The cave sits on the border of [Hjaalmarch](/wiki/Skyrim:Hjaalmarch "Skyrim:Hjaalmarch") and [the Reach](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Reach "Skyrim:The Reach") next to a small waterfall and pond, explaining the water-filled channels within the cave. The pond contains [slaughterfish](/wiki/Skyrim:Slaughterfish "Skyrim:Slaughterfish") and their accompanying [eggs](/wiki/Skyrim:Slaughterfish_Egg "Skyrim:Slaughterfish Egg"). The entrance to the cave is illuminated by a brazier, and samples of [bleeding crown](/wiki/Skyrim:Bleeding_Crown "Skyrim:Bleeding Crown"), [mora tapinella](/wiki/Skyrim:Mora_Tapinella "Skyrim:Mora Tapinella"), and [lavender](/wiki/Skyrim:Lavender "Skyrim:Lavender") can be found growing in the area. A [bear](/wiki/Skyrim:Bear "Skyrim:Bear") may be prowling the exterior of the cave.

### Chillwind Depths

Chillwind Depths interior

Chillwind Depths is inhabited by Falmer and infested with frostbite spiders. It is a system of mostly water-logged tunnels, a prime environment for many of the fungi found in Skyrim. The entrance is a downward slope lined with bleeding crown, [fly amanita](/wiki/Skyrim:Fly_Amanita "Skyrim:Fly Amanita"), imp stool, and Namira's rot. It leads down to a partially submerged narrow cavern. Foremost is a small campsite with the body of an adventurer by the campfire. The chest in his campsite has been looted, but there is a [potion of healing](/wiki/Skyrim:Potion_of_Healing "Skyrim:Potion of Healing"), some [cabbage soup](/wiki/Skyrim:Cabbage_Soup "Skyrim:Cabbage Soup"), and a [horker loaf](/wiki/Skyrim:Horker_Loaf "Skyrim:Horker Loaf") on the small rock ledge. With the [Fishing](/wiki/Skyrim:Fishing "Skyrim:Fishing") [Creation](/wiki/Skyrim:Creation_Club "Skyrim:Creation Club") installed, this camp also has some [Fishing Supplies](/wiki/Skyrim:Fishing_Supplies "Skyrim:Fishing Supplies"). Fish from [Underground](/wiki/Skyrim:Fishing_(activity)#Biomes "Skyrim:Fishing (activity)") waters can be caught here.

As you wade through the knee-deep water, heading south, notice the proliferation of spider webs. Indeed, where the path becomes extremely narrow, a short passage on the right opens up. This leads to a small nest where one frostbite spider is keeping watch over five [web sacs](/wiki/Skyrim:Web_Sac "Skyrim:Web Sac") containing [spider eggs](/wiki/Skyrim:Spider_Egg "Skyrim:Spider Egg"). There are also two burned corpses entangled in the webbing. At the back of the nest, a dense buildup of webbing can be cut through to reveal a [battleaxe](/wiki/Skyrim:Battleaxe "Skyrim:Battleaxe"). There is also a cluster of blisterwort and fly amanita growing at the entrance of the passage and against the back wall.

Back in the main tunnel, continue south until the tunnel opens to a cavern. The trail leads out of the water, onto higher ground and into four waiting frostbite spiders. Numerous web sacs hang from the ceiling, and there are six clusters of blisterwort growing in this cavern. A cluster of Namira's rot is growing to the left on the shore, and a cluster of imp stool grows on the right. An accessible web sac is hanging from the western wall, and across from it, illuminated by lantern light and amid clusters of blisterwort, is the body of another unlucky adventurer. Fight your way uphill to the exit, another narrow tunnel heading northeast. Burnt corpses tangled in webbing line this short tunnel. Samples of blisterwort, Namira's rot, imp stool, and white cap also grow along the walls. More web sacs hang from above. The tunnel takes a sharp turn to the east, and the water begins to flow again. Here you face a fork in the path, with the choice of going left to the north or straight heading southeast. The path to the left heading north is lined with imp stool and fly amanita. The trail leads downward, becoming submerged, but with enough headroom to breathe. As the trail turns back to the east, it becomes totally submerged, but there is a short enough distance to the other end that [waterbreathing](/wiki/Skyrim:Waterbreathing_(effect) "Skyrim:Waterbreathing (effect)") is not necessary. You will surface in another water-filled grotto with roots hanging from the ceiling, but enough headroom to breathe. Immediately to your left, on the north wall, take a short dunk underwater to find a submerged apprentice-locked chest. The exit out is on the south wall, and is another fully submerged tunnel. It is swimmable without a breathing aid, and heads south then turns upwards to the west. This tunnel emerges back onto the main trail again, the same as if you had gone straight southeast, back at the fork. You may therefore choose to save yourself some swimming, get the loot from the locked submerged chest, backtrack to the main passage, and take the trail heading southeast. You will see the tunnel opening to the underwater passage on your right as you proceed.

A frostbite spider is a short distance ahead. Next, straight ahead, two Falmer are guarding the trail, each perched on a rocky outcrop. Samples of all the mushrooms are growing along this tunnel, and when the trail takes a slight turn to the west, [glowing mushrooms](/wiki/Skyrim:Glowing_Mushroom "Skyrim:Glowing Mushroom") are growing on the wall to your left. Another Falmer is patrolling here as well. This is also the entryway into the Falmer settlement. A [pressure plate](/wiki/Skyrim:Pressure_Plate "Skyrim:Pressure Plate") triggering a [spear trap](/wiki/Skyrim:Spear_Trap "Skyrim:Spear Trap") is just at the mouth of the cave. The next room is small, but contains an abundance of all the mushrooms, and given the baskets scattered about, apparently serves as a mushroom farm. A Falmer and a chaurus/spider are also here awaiting your arrival. Continuing on through another waterlogged narrow passage, you will encounter another Falmer and a frostbite spider; after disposing of them, you can mine an [orichalcum ore vein](/wiki/Skyrim:Orichalcum_Ore_Vein "Skyrim:Orichalcum Ore Vein") found on the left-hand side of the passage. As the passage turns to the north, the path forks into two: a lower path continuing straight ahead through the shallow water, and a rocky incline ascending along the right-hand wall. There is a Falmer waiting on the rocky ledge of the incline, and at least two more Falmer are straight ahead. Fighting your way through the water takes you through a very narrow passage to the Falmer camp. Fighting through here, while essentially bottle-necking your opponents, does not give you much room to maneuver, and leads to an all-out assault on the camp. A stealthier method is to take the rocky incline up and across the tunnel into a more secluded area of the camp with only a single Falmer hut. Here another Falmer is looking for you. In this campsite are two tables; the table on the right has three [chaurus chitin](/wiki/Skyrim:Chaurus_Chitin "Skyrim:Chaurus Chitin") and two [iron ores](/wiki/Skyrim:Iron_Ore "Skyrim:Iron Ore"), and the table on the left has a [Falmer shield](/wiki/Skyrim:Falmer_Shield "Skyrim:Falmer Shield"), two [Falmer swords](/wiki/Skyrim:Falmer_Sword "Skyrim:Falmer Sword"), and two [Falmer helmets](/wiki/Skyrim:Falmer_Helmet "Skyrim:Falmer Helmet"). Inside the hut is a potion. Among the various samples of mushrooms here, five samples of glowing mushrooms can be collected. There is also an orichalcum ore vein on the north wall, across from the hut. Depending on your [sneak](/wiki/Skyrim:Sneak "Skyrim:Sneak") level and the row you make up here, another Falmer and a chaurus may come to investigate. After all is clear, continue down the slope to the main camp.

The first structure you come to on the right is the chaurus corral with a leveled chaurus as sentry. Inside the corral are over eighty [egg sacs](/wiki/Skyrim:Egg_Sac "Skyrim:Egg Sac") containing [chaurus eggs](/wiki/Skyrim:Chaurus_Eggs "Skyrim:Chaurus Eggs"). The body of a prisoner floats in the shallow water. From the gate of the corral, turn left, heading northeast. (Going right takes you back out to the main passage, just below the ramp leading up.) Pick off at least four more Falmer as you make your way through the settlement, at least two of which are sniping at you from above on a rocky ledge. A Falmer chest is on the right, under a rocky ledge. Straight ahead are four prisoner holding pens. The first pen on the left holds the body of a man named [Firir](/wiki/Skyrim:Firir "Skyrim:Firir"). Looting him results in some gold and a [torn note](/wiki/Skyrim:Torn_Note "Skyrim:Torn Note") in which he describes the horrors of this place and pleads for forgiveness from [Eydis](/wiki/Skyrim:Eydis "Skyrim:Eydis"). The next pen holds another prisoner's body and some glowing mushrooms. The pen directly across is empty, other than some Namira's rot and imp stool. The last pen has an expert-locked Falmer chest. Turn back, heading south, but veer left onto the shore and up the incline where the two Falmer were shooting at you.

On this rise is another Falmer campsite. Other than a [skeever](/wiki/Skyrim:Charred_Skeever_Meat "Skyrim:Charred Skeever Meat") charring over the fire, there is nothing of interest in this camp. From the top of the incline, make a hairpin turn, heading north to continue. From this position, you will witness a leveled Falmer performing some sort of ritual over the body of another prisoner. A [Falmer hive](/wiki/Skyrim:Falmer_Hive "Skyrim:Falmer Hive") is on the wall to the left, so keep an eye out for emerging Falmer. Slopes on either side of the stone table lead down to a sunken retention pond with numerous chaurus egg sacs and glowing mushrooms. The boss Falmer may retreat when he sees you, fleeing across the bridge to the far side of the cavern. After defeating him, continue down the narrow path to the boss campsite. A coin purse is on a rock shelf on the right. Ahead is a table with a copy of the [Lockpicking](/wiki/Skyrim:Lockpicking "Skyrim:Lockpicking") [skill book](/wiki/Skyrim:Skill_Books "Skyrim:Skill Books") *[Advances in Lockpicking](/wiki/Skyrim:Advances_in_Lockpicking "Skyrim:Advances in Lockpicking")*, an [apothecary's satchel](/wiki/Skyrim:Apothecary%27s_Satchel "Skyrim:Apothecary's Satchel"), a [warhammer](/wiki/Skyrim:Warhammer "Skyrim:Warhammer"), and a [helmet](/wiki/Skyrim:Helmet "Skyrim:Helmet"). To the left of the table is the boss Falmer chest. A potion is next to the chest. The path out is to the east, leading you to a small ledge. Jump down to the water below to find yourself back at the main entrance to the cave, by the first unfortunate adventurer's camp.

## Notes

- A [Solitude guard](/wiki/Skyrim:Solitude_Guard "Skyrim:Solitude Guard") will sometimes remark, "*The road to Whiterun's not safe these days. Lots of travelers just... disappear, south of Dragon Bridge. Can't find a trace of them.*" A map marker for Chillwind Depths will be added when this occurs.
- An *[Adventurer's Journal](/wiki/Skyrim:Adventurer%27s_Journal "Skyrim:Adventurer's Journal")* in an abandoned camp down along the river, just across from the main road, tells of the adventurer's curiosity regarding an attack on a trade caravan and his intention to investigate, leading him to this cave. With the Fishing Creation installed, this camp has some Fishing Supplies.
- There is a dead Redguard and Nord surrounded by Falmer arrows lying next to a wagon and a dead horse to the northeast across the river from the abandoned camp. The Redguard woman carries a *[Merchant's Journal](/wiki/Skyrim:Merchant%27s_Journal "Skyrim:Merchant's Journal")* referring to attacks on trade caravans.
- There is a pillar just inside the cave. You can circle around and jump onto the pillar, then use the [Whirlwind Sprint](/wiki/Skyrim:Whirlwind_Sprint "Skyrim:Whirlwind Sprint") [shout](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Shouts "Skyrim:Dragon Shouts") to fly through the doorway across a small gap and loot the final room while avoiding most or all enemies in the cave.
- Chillwind Depths also [appears](/wiki/Online:Chillwind_Depths "Online:Chillwind Depths") in [ESO](/wiki/Online:Online "Online:Online").

## Maps

- 

  Chillwind Depths

Wood chopping block

### Easy Money

If you talk to one of the quest givers, they will offer to pay you for chopped [firewood](/wiki/Skyrim:Firewood "Skyrim:Firewood"). Alternatively, you can also chop the firewood first and then sell the firewood to a quest giver later. You are paid five gold per unit of firewood.

### Find a Chopping Block

As a general rule, wood chopping blocks are easily found near the quest givers. Otherwise, they can be found in almost any [military camp](/wiki/Category:Skyrim-Places-Military_Camps "Category:Skyrim-Places-Military Camps") or [Khajiit traders](/wiki/Skyrim:Khajiit_Traders "Skyrim:Khajiit Traders") caravan camp, and also at the following locations:

| [Winterhold](/wiki/Skyrim:Winterhold_(region) "Skyrim:Winterhold (region)") | [Bloodchill Cavern](/wiki/Skyrim:Bloodchill_Cavern "Skyrim:Bloodchill Cavern")([CC](/wiki/Skyrim:Bloodchill_Manor "Skyrim:Bloodchill Manor")) |

### Get Chopping

To chop wood you must have a [woodcutter's axe](/wiki/Skyrim:Woodcutter%27s_Axe "Skyrim:Woodcutter's Axe") in your inventory (one can usually be found near the wood pile). In addition to standard woodcutter's axes, the [Poacher's Axe](/wiki/Skyrim:Poacher%27s_Axe "Skyrim:Poacher's Axe") can be used to chop firewood. Activating a wood chopping block will then cause you to produce firewood at a rate of two units every eight seconds, with a limit of six units per activation. After you have produced six units, you must activate the block again or leave the woodcutting session. You can leave partially through, in which you'll either cut two or four units instead.

It is also possible to have a [follower](/wiki/Skyrim:Followers "Skyrim:Followers") chop firewood for you, even if they don't have an axe. By having someone else do the chopping, you can perform other tasks such as smithing and selling items. By multitasking and restarting their orders every few moments, you can earn several hundred gold on the side while performing bartering.

If a second wood chopping block is nearby, you can chop wood simultaneously to double production while only adding an extra couple of seconds to the equation. This can be done early on in [Riverwood](/wiki/Skyrim:Riverwood "Skyrim:Riverwood") by getting [Faendal](/wiki/Skyrim:Faendal "Skyrim:Faendal") as a follower and then using the two chopping blocks near the mill. Use the command feature to command Faendal from afar and maximize efficiency. After twenty or so minutes of woodcutting, you can earn a few thousand gold at the beginning of the game without gaining any XP.

## Achievements

An [Achievement](/wiki/Skyrim:Achievements "Skyrim:Achievements") is related to chopping wood:

-  **Hard Worker** (10 points/Bronze) — Chop wood, [mine ore](/wiki/Skyrim:Mining "Skyrim:Mining"), and [cook food](/wiki/Skyrim:Cooking "Skyrim:Cooking")
  - To obtain this achievement you do not need to sell the firewood, or even talk to any of the quest givers. Simply activating the wood chopping block is sufficient.

## Notes

- This quest does not have any stages or objectives.
- This quest can be repeated indefinitely.
- There is no limit to the amount of firewood you can chop at each wood chopping block and then sell. One (painfully slow) way to get the money to purchase a house is to chop the required amount of wood. For the house in Whiterun, for example, you will get 5000 gold if you accumulate 1000 pieces of firewood. This takes approximately 24 hours of game time when the time scale is set around 10, or 25 minutes in real time. At the standard time scale, it is possible to chop 150 pieces of firewood in 15 real-time minutes, which is a pay rate of 3000 gold per real-time hour.
- You can also ask a follower to chop wood for you, by entering [command](/wiki/Skyrim:Followers#Commands "Skyrim:Followers") mode and selecting a valid chopping block. The follower does not need to be carrying a woodcutter's axe to perform this. They will begin a single cycle of the chopping animation (3 chops gaining 6 wood) before returning to standing idle. They can continue to chop even when they are overencumbered.
  - As an augmented way to make money, you can find a location which has two chopping blocks nearby, command your follower to use one, and use the other yourself. This will nearly double your output and allow earning a sizable amount of gold in less time.
    - [Riverwood](/wiki/Skyrim:Riverwood "Skyrim:Riverwood") is the easiest location to do this, as it has two blocks, is accessible immediately at the start of the game, and even provides [Faendal](/wiki/Skyrim:Faendal "Skyrim:Faendal") as an easy-to-get follower to help you chop wood. Note that the follower will need to be reinstructed to chop wood each time they finish, so there is a bit of micromanagement involved. When your character finishes his/her own chopping cycle, return to the follower and repeat the process.
- A less tedious method of earning passive gold is simply telling your follower to chop wood while you are in a city or settlement, checking in every once in a while as you go about your business.
- Money you earn from chopping wood is fixed and is not affected by your [Speech](/wiki/Skyrim:Speech "Skyrim:Speech") skill. This makes the quest one of the few ways to [make money](/wiki/Skyrim:Making_Money "Skyrim:Making Money") without increasing any skills, which will help control your level. This is useful when wanting to [train](/wiki/Skyrim:Trainers "Skyrim:Trainers") in a certain skill as many times as possible. It is also one of the few ways to earn money without doing any questing, merchanting, or crafting.
- With the [Hearthfire](/wiki/Skyrim:Hearthfire "Skyrim:Hearthfire") add-on, doing this quest for [Aeri](/wiki/Skyrim:Aeri "Skyrim:Aeri"), [Gilfre](/wiki/Skyrim:Gilfre "Skyrim:Gilfre"), [Grosta](/wiki/Skyrim:Grosta "Skyrim:Grosta"), [Hert](/wiki/Skyrim:Hert "Skyrim:Hert"), or [Hod](/wiki/Skyrim:Hod "Skyrim:Hod") will increase their disposition such that you'll be able to [cut your own lumber](/wiki/Skyrim:Cutting_Lumber "Skyrim:Cutting Lumber") for [construction](/wiki/Skyrim:Construction "Skyrim:Construction") purposes.
- Because this is a favor quest which affects the quest giver's disposition, it will count towards the "Help the People" part of the [thane](/wiki/Skyrim:Thane "Skyrim:Thane") quest for the quest giver's hold.
- Each unit of firewood weighs 5, and a full use of the chopping block gives 6 wood, for a total weight of 30. If you become overencumbered, which will happen rather quickly, you can drop the entire stack of wood and pick it up by holding the "grab" button to be able to run over to the person to whom you wish to sell it.
- Swinging the woodcutter's axe at a chopping block won't produce firewood; you must activate the animation sequence.
- Firewood samples found in the wilderness can also be used. Despite the abundance of wood piles which use the same model, these standalone samples can be quite rare. [Autumnwatch Tower](/wiki/Skyrim:Autumnwatch_Tower "Skyrim:Autumnwatch Tower") has three firewood scattered over the floors of the tallest tower. Given the sheer weight of the wood and the fact that only a handful of NPCs will buy firewood at-cost, it is probably not worth the effort to grab these scattered pieces, unless you have a follower to bear the burden.
  - Like other [gathering quests](/wiki/Skyrim:Gather_Wheat "Skyrim:Gather Wheat"), NPCs do not care if the firewood is stolen.
- Some objects in the game world look like wood chopping blocks, but aren't. If it lacks one or both piles of wood along the sides of it, it is not a wood chopping block. When scrolling over a usable block, the "Activate" prompt will appear.
-  Version 1.2.4 of the [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch") adds woodcutter's axes next to the wood piles in Whiterun, Riften, and Windhelm so that being asked to chop wood won't result in you needing to exit the city and travel to a nearby village just to get an axe.
  -  Version 2.1.2 of the Unofficial Skyrim Patch adds woodcutter's axes next to the wood piles in Kynesgrove, Dragon Bridge, Ivarstead, and Half-Moon Mill for essentially the same reason.
- Time doesn't stop while chopping wood so magicka, health, and stamina regenerate while using a chopping block.
- Chopped wood can be sold to general goods merchants, though at a much lower price than someone on the list above.

# Skyrim:Christer

## Overview

| Christer (RefID: 0009073E) | | | |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Location | [Mistwatch North Tower](/wiki/Skyrim:Mistwatch_North_Tower "Skyrim:Mistwatch North Tower") | | |
| Race | [Nord](/wiki/Skyrim:Nord "Skyrim:Nord") | Gender | Male |
| Level | 1 | Class | [Food Vendor](/wiki/Skyrim:Food_Vendor "Skyrim:Food Vendor") |
| [RefID](/wiki/Skyrim:NPCs#Console_IDs "Skyrim:NPCs") | 0009073E | [BaseID](/wiki/Skyrim:NPCs#Console_IDs "Skyrim:NPCs") | 00090738 |
| Other Information | | | |
| [Health](/wiki/Skyrim:Health "Skyrim:Health") | 50 | [Magicka](/wiki/Skyrim:Magicka "Skyrim:Magicka") | 50 |
| [Stamina](/wiki/Skyrim:Stamina "Skyrim:Stamina") | 50 | | |
| Primary [Skills](/wiki/Skyrim:Skills "Skyrim:Skills") | [Two-handed](/wiki/Skyrim:Two-handed "Skyrim:Two-handed") | | |

| Voice Type | [MaleCoward](/wiki/Category:Skyrim-Voice-MaleCoward "Category:Skyrim-Voice-MaleCoward") | | |

Christer

**Christer** is a [Nord](/wiki/Skyrim:Nord "Skyrim:Nord") who is searching for his wife, [Fjola](/wiki/Skyrim:Fjola "Skyrim:Fjola"). He believes her to be a hostage in the [Mistwatch](/wiki/Skyrim:Mistwatch "Skyrim:Mistwatch") bandit stronghold, and offers a reward if she can be rescued.

Christer wears a pair of [boots](/wiki/Skyrim:Boots#000209a5 "Skyrim:Boots"), a set of [clothes](/wiki/Skyrim:Clothes#000209a6 "Skyrim:Clothes"), and a [hat](/wiki/Skyrim:Hat#000209aa "Skyrim:Hat"). He carries no items.

Christer will spend all of his time in a supply closet near the entrance to the Mistwatch North Tower. If you convince him to leave, he runs to the exit, never to be seen again after he leaves.

## Related Quests

- **[Mistwatch](/wiki/Skyrim:Mistwatch_(quest) "Skyrim:Mistwatch (quest)")**: Help Christer locate his kidnapped wife [Fjola](/wiki/Skyrim:Fjola "Skyrim:Fjola").

### Mistwatch

After entering Mistwatch, Christer will call out to you by saying:

:   *"Hey, who's there?"*

After a moment, he will ask that you come speak to him:

:   *"You - over here, quick. Before any of them show up!"*

Continuing to stall will have him tell you that he needs assistance:

:   *"Please, stranger! I need your help!"*

Approaching Christer will have him ask for your assistance:

:   *"Stendarr's mercy - you aren't one of them. Please, you've got to help me!"*
:   **What's going on?**
:   *"It's my wife, Fjola! I think she's being held in this tower."*
:   **Calm down. Just tell me what happened.**
:   *"I'm sorry, I'm just... you're right. Let me explain. Fjola, my wife, left the farm on errands and never came back. It's been months, and I've been searching for her since. I heard a rumor that these bandits were ransoming captives, so I thought she may be here. I managed to sneak past the guards and get this far, but... I don't think I can go on. I'm no warrior! Please, can you look for her?"*

:   :   **You're sure she's being held here?**
    :   *"Honestly? I have no idea. But I've looked all over and the kidnappings here started around when she disappeared. So I have to hope..."*

:   :   **Very well. I'll look for her.**
    :   *"Thank you! I don't have much, but I can give you some coin for the trouble. One of the guards dropped this key while I hid. I wager it will come in handy for you. Please hurry!"*

Speaking to Christer before discovering Fjola will have him claim that he does not wish to speak to you until Fjola is found:

:   *"Until you can find out whether Fjola is here there's nothing I care to to*[[sic](/wiki/UESPWiki:Spelling#Books_and_Direct_Quotes "UESPWiki:Spelling")] *discuss."*

Returning to Christer after killing the Bandit Leader or agreeing to lie to Christer will have him question why Fjola isn't with you:

:   *"What news? Why isn't Fjola with you?"*

If you listened to Fjola, you will have two dialogue options, though Christer will be pleased either way:

:   :   **She's dead, but I found this.**
    :   *"That... I gave it to her on our wedding day. Help me, Divines... it's true isn't it? I'm sorry. Keep the ring. I cannot bear the weight of them in my heart, and I must make the journey alone now. Thank you for... thank you."*

:   :   **I found this ring, but no sign of her.**
    :   *"Her marriage band? Then there's hope - she was here! I have to move on if I want to find her. Please, take the coin I promised. Blessings of Stendarr on you!"*

If you killed Fjola, you will only have this dialogue option, and Christer will immediately become hostile:

:   :   **I had to kill her. She attacked me.**
    :   *"What? My Fjola would never... You monster! I'll kill you for this!"*

If you killed Fjola and told Christer that you had to kill her you can proceed with casting a calm spell on him, leave the interior and come back, this way you get to pick one of the other two options instead.

# Skyrim:Cicero

## Overview

| Cicero (RefID: 0009BCB0) ([lore page](/wiki/Lore:Cicero "Lore:Cicero")) | | | |
